style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Isinglass-Wins-The-De.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/54/Isinglass-Wins-The-De.jpg/220px-Isinglass-Wins-The-De.jpg" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/54/Isinglass-Wins-The-De.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="283" data-file-height="170" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Isinglass-Wins-The-De.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Isinglass_(horse)" title="Isinglass (horse)">Isinglass</a> wins the Derby</i> (1893)</div></div></div>\n<p>The <b>Derby Stakes</b>, officially the <b>Investec Derby</b>, popularly known as <b>the Derby</b>, is a <a href="/wiki/Conditions_races" title="Conditions races">Group 1</a> <a href="/wiki/Flat_racing" title="Flat racing">flat</a> <a href="/wiki/Horse_racing" title="Horse racing">horse race</a> in England open to three-year-old <a href="/wiki/Thoroughbred" title="Thoroughbred">thoroughbred</a> <a href="/wiki/Colt_(horse)" title="Colt (horse)">colts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Filly" title="Filly">fillies</a>. It is run at <a href="/wiki/Epsom_Downs_Racecourse" title="Epsom Downs Racecourse">Epsom Downs Racecourse</a> in Surrey over a distance of one mile, four <a href="/wiki/Furlong" title="Furlong">furlongs</a> and 6 yards (2,420 metres), on the first Saturday of June each year.<sup id="cite_ref-century_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-century-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It is Britain\'s richest horse race, and the most prestigious of the five <a href="/wiki/British_Classic_Races" title="British Classic Races">Classics</a>. It is sometimes referred to as the "Blue Riband" of the turf. The race serves as the middle leg of the <a href="/wiki/Triple_Crown_of_Thoroughbred_Racing#United_Kingdom" title="Triple Crown of Thoroughbred Racing">Triple Crown</a>, preceded by the <a href="/wiki/2000_Guineas_Stakes" title="2000 Guineas Stakes">2000 Guineas</a> and followed by the <a href="/wiki/St_Leger_Stakes" title="St Leger Stakes">St&#160;Leger</a>. Owners rarely try to have their horses win all three races any more, as it is hard on the horses. \n</p><p>The name "Derby" has become synonymous with great races all over the world, and as such has been borrowed many times, notably by the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Derby" title="Kentucky Derby">Kentucky Derby</a> in the United States. The Derby run at Epsom is the original and in Great Britain is invariably referred to as "the Derby". It is one of Britain\'s great national sporting events<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and has a large worldwide TV audience.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Epsom_Fair"><span class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Records"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Records</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Winners"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Epsom_Derby&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Stanley family, Earls of Derby, had a long history of horse-racing, and <a href="/wiki/James_Stanley,_7th_Earl_of_Derby" title="James Stanley, 7th Earl of Derby">James Stanley, 7th Earl of Derby</a>, who gained the Lordship of Mann in 1627, instituted horse-racing on the <a href="/wiki/Langness_Peninsula" title="Langness Peninsula">Langness Peninsula</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>, donating a cup for what became known as the "<a href="/wiki/Manx_Derby" title="Manx Derby">Manx Derby</a>". <sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Derby originated at a celebration following the first running of the <a href="/wiki/Epsom_Oaks" title="Epsom Oaks">Oaks Stakes</a> in 1779. A new race was planned, and it was decided that it should be named after either the host of the party, the <a href="/wiki/Edward_Smith-Stanley,_12th_Earl_of_Derby" title="Edward Smith-Stanley, 12th Earl of Derby">12th Earl of Derby</a>, or one of his guests, <a href="/wiki/Sir_Charles_Bunbury,_6th_Baronet" title="Sir Charles Bunbury, 6th Baronet">Sir Charles Bunbury</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Bunbury_Cup" title="Bunbury Cup">Bunbury Cup</a> run at Newmarket would later be named in his honour). According to legend the decision was made by the toss of a coin, but it is probable that Bunbury, the Steward of the <a href="/wiki/Jockey_Club" title="Jockey Club">Jockey Club</a>, deferred to his host.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The inaugural running of the Derby was held on Thursday 4 May 1780. It was won by <a href="/wiki/Diomed" title="Diomed">Diomed</a>, a colt owned by Sir Charles Bunbury, who collected prize money of \xc2\xa31,065 15s. The first four runnings were contested over 1 mile, but this was amended to the current distance of 1\xc2\xbd miles in 1784. Lord Derby achieved his first success in the event in 1787, with a horse called <a href="/wiki/Sir_Peter_Teazle" title="Sir Peter Teazle">Sir Peter Teazle</a>.\n</p><p>The starting point of the race was moved twice during the 19th century. The first move, suggested by <a href="/wiki/Lord_George_Bentinck" title="Lord George Bentinck">Lord George Bentinck</a>, was in 1848, and the second was in 1872. It was discovered in 1991 that the exact length of the race was one mile, four furlongs and 10 yards.<sup id="cite_ref-century_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-century-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Initially, the Derby was run on a Thursday in late May or early June, depending on when Easter occurred. In 1838 the race was moved to a Wednesday to fit in with the railways\' <a href="/wiki/Timetables" class="mw-redirect" title="Timetables">timetables</a>, but still followed the moveable feast of Easter. In the 20th century, the race was run on the first Wednesday in June from 1900 until 1995, not including 1915 to 1918 (during the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>), when it was on a Tuesday. During the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, from 1942 until 1945 the race was run on a Saturday, as it was in the post-war years of 1947 to 1950 and again in 1953.<sup id="cite_ref-century_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-century-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> In 1995 the day was changed from the first Wednesday in June to the first Saturday,<sup id="cite_ref-SpiritsUp_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpiritsUp-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and since then all the races have taken place on that day.\n</p><p>The Derby has been run at Epsom in all years except during the <a href="/wiki/World_war" title="World war">world wars</a>. From 1915 to 1918 and from 1940 to 1945, the Derby was run at <a href="/wiki/Newmarket_Racecourse" title="Newmarket Racecourse">Newmarket</a>. These races are known as the \'New Derby\'.\n</p><p>The Derby has inspired many similar events around the world. European variations include the <a href="/wiki/Derby_Italiano" title="Derby Italiano">Derby Italiano</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Deutsches_Derby" title="Deutsches Derby">Deutsches Derby</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Derby" title="Irish Derby">Irish Derby</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Prix_du_Jockey_Club" title="Prix du Jockey Club">Prix du Jockey Club</a> (popularly known in the British Isles as the "French Derby"). Several races in the United States include the "Derby" name, including the oldest, the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Derby" title="Kentucky Derby">Kentucky Derby</a>. Other national equivalents include the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Derby" title="Australian Derby">Australian Derby</a>, the <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Derby" title="New Zealand Derby">New Zealand Derby</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Y%C5%ABshun" title="Tokyo Y\xc5\xabshun">Tokyo Y\xc5\xabshun</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Epsom_Fair">Epsom Fair</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Epsom_Derby&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Epsom Fair">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Powell_Frith_-_The_Derby_Day_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/William_Powell_Frith_-_The_Derby_Day_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/220px-William_Powell_Frith_-_The_Derby_Day_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" width="220" height="97" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/William_Powell_Frith_-_The_Derby_Day_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/330px-William_Powell_Frith_-_The_Derby_Day_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/William_Powell_Frith_-_The_Derby_Day_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/440px-William_Powell_Frith_-_The_Derby_Day_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4001" data-file-height="1761" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Powell_Frith_-_The_Derby_Day_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/The_Derby_Day" title="The Derby Day">The Derby Day</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/William_Powell_Frith" title="William Powell Frith">William Powell Frith</a> (1858)</div></div></div>\n<p>For many years the Derby was run on a Wednesday or a Thursday and on the day huge crowds would come from London, not only to see the race but to enjoy other entertainment (during some of the 19th century and most of the 20th Parliament would adjourn to allow members to attend the meeting).<sup id="cite_ref-SpiritsUp_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpiritsUp-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Malden_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Malden-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the time that <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens">Charles Dickens</a> visited Epsom Downs to view the race in the 1850s, entertainers such as musicians, clowns, and conjurers plied their trades and entertained the crowds; other forms of entertainment included coconut stalls.<sup id="cite_ref-Crane_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crane-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The crowded meeting was the subject of a painting by <a href="/wiki/William_Powell_Frith" title="William Powell Frith">William Powell Frith</a> painted in the 1858 and titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Derby_Day" title="The Derby Day">The Derby Day</a></i>; critics have noted that the foreground of the painting features the entertainment attractions, while the racing is relegated to the margins.<sup id="cite_ref-Payne_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Payne-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 1870s, the <a href="/wiki/Stationary_steam_engine" title="Stationary steam engine">steam-driven</a> rides were introduced. They were located at the <a href="/wiki/Tattenham_Corner" title="Tattenham Corner">Tattenham Corner</a> end of the grounds and the fair was on for ten days and entertained hundreds of thousands.<sup id="cite_ref-Crane_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crane-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> During the latter half of the 20th century, Derby Day became less popular and the race was moved from Wednesday to Saturday in 1995 the hope of reviving high attendance.<sup id="cite_ref-SpiritsUp_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpiritsUp-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> As the number of people attending the fair dwindled in the face of competition for attention and changing tastes, its length was reduced from 10 days to three or four.<sup id="cite_ref-Crane_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crane-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorship">Sponsorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Epsom_Derby&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Sponsorship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Investec" title="Investec">Investec</a> became the sponsor of the Derby in 2009, and the current sponsorship deal runs until 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The race was previously backed by <a href="/wiki/Energizer_Holdings" class="mw-redirect" title="Energizer Holdings">Ever Ready</a> (1984\xe2\x80\x9394) and <a href="/wiki/Vodafone" title="Vodafone">Vodafone</a> (1995\xe2\x80\x932008).<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Popular_culture">Popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Epsom_Derby&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>The 1952 drama film <i><a href="/wiki/Derby_Day_(1952_film)" title="Derby Day (1952 film)">Derby Day</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Wilcox" title="Herbert Wilcox">Herbert Wilcox</a> and starring <a href="/wiki/Michael_Wilding_(actor)" title="Michael Wilding (actor)">Michael Wilding</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anna_Neagle" title="Anna Neagle">Anna Neagle</a>, is set entirely around The Derby.</li></ul>\n<p>Epsom Derby is also referenced in the recent popular BBC television series <i><a href="/wiki/Peaky_Blinders" title="Peaky Blinders">Peaky Blinders</a></i>, set in the 20th century.\n</p>\n<table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="clear:right; float:right; text-align:center; font-weight:bold;">\n<caption style="border:1px solid black; background-color: (1976), The Minstrel (1977), Teenoso (1983)</i></li></ul>\n<p><b>Leading <a href="/wiki/Horse_trainer" title="Horse trainer">trainer</a> (7 wins):</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Robson" (1938), Pont l\'Eveque (1940), Owen Tudor (1941)</i><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;N 1&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p><b>Leading owner (7 wins):</b> <i>1\xc2\xbd</i>\n</td>\n<td><span style="display:none">154.93</span> 2:34.93\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><span style="font-size:85%">\n<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_dista"><a href="#ref_dista"><b><sup>a</sup></b></a></span>  Winning distances are shown in <a href="/wiki/Horse_length" title="Horse length">lengths</a> or shorter (<b>dh</b> = dead-heat; <b>shd</b> = short-head; <b>hd</b> = head; <b>snk</b> = short-neck; <b>nk</b> = neck).\n<br />\n<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_1828b"><a href="#ref_1828b"><b><sup>b</sup></b></a></span>  The 1828 race finished as a dead-heat, but Cadland won a run-off against <a href="/wiki/The_Colonel_(horse)" title="The Colonel (horse)">The Colonel</a> by \xc2\xbd length.\n<br />\n<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_1844c"><a href="#ref_1844c"><b><sup>c</sup></b></a></span> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_1913d"><a href="#ref_1913d"><b><sup>d</sup></b></a></span>  The 1844 and 1913 winners were awarded victory after the disqualification of the first-placed horse.\n</span>\n</p>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid gray; background-color: #e2e2e2; color:black; font-size:80%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160; Wartime substitute race at <a href="/wiki/Newmarket_Racecourse" title="Newmarket Racecourse">Newmarket</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Timeline">Timeline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Epsom_Derby&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Timeline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amato.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Amato.jpg/220px-Amato.jpg" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Amato.jpg/330px-Amato.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Amato.jpg/440px-Amato.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="383" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amato.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Amato_(racehorse)" class="mw-redirect" title="Amato (racehorse)"><i>Amato</i></a>, 1838 Derby winner by <a href="/wiki/John_Frederick_Herring,_Sr." class="mw-redirect" title="John Frederick Herring, Sr.">John Frederick Herring, Sr</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shirley_Heights.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Shirley_Heights.jpg/220px-Shirley_Heights.jpg" width="220" height="278" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Shirley_Heights.jpg/330px-Shirley_Heights.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Shirley_Heights.jpg/440px-Shirley_Heights.jpg 2x" data-file-width="590" data-file-height="745" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shirley_Heights.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Shirley_Heights_(horse)" title="Shirley Heights (horse)">Shirley Heights</a></i>, 1978 Derby winner by <a href="/wiki/Bob_Demuyser" class="mw-redirect" title="Bob Demuyser">Bob Demuyser</a> (1920\xe2\x80\x932003)</div></div></div>\n<ul><li><b>1805</b>: One of the horses was brought down by a spectator.</li>\n<li><b>1825</b>: Middleton never raced before or after winning the Derby.</li>\n<li><b>1838</b>: <a href="/wiki/Amato_(racehorse)" class="mw-redirect" title="Amato (racehorse)">Amato</a> never raced before or after winning the Derby.</li>\n<li><b>1844</b>: The original winner Running Rein was disqualified as he was actually an ineligible four-year-old horse named Maccabeus.<sup id="cite_ref-Foulkes_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Foulkes-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>1881</b>: <a href="/wiki/Iroquois_(horse)" title="Iroquois (horse)">Iroquois</a> became the first American-bred to win a leg of the British triple crown.</li>\n<li><b>1884</b>: The race finished with a dead-heat between <a href="/wiki/Harvester_(horse)" title="Harvester (horse)">Harvester</a> and St. Gatien.</li>\n<li><b>1887</b>: Merry Hampton is the most recent horse to win the Derby with no previous victories.</li>\n<li><b>1894</b>: The winner was owned by the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister</a> at the time, the <a href="/wiki/Archibald_Primrose,_5th_Earl_of_Rosebery" title="Archibald Primrose, 5th Earl of Rosebery">5th Earl of Rosebery</a>.</li>\n<li><b>1901</b>: The first year in which a mechanical starting gate was used.</li>\n<li><b>1909</b>: Minoru was the first Derby winner owned by a reigning monarch, <a href="/wiki/Edward_VII_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward VII of the United Kingdom">King Edward VII</a>, who had previously won twice as <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales" title="Prince of Wales">Prince of Wales</a>.</li>\n<li><b>1913</b>: The 6/4 favourite Craganour, owned by Charles B. Ismay, brother of <a href="/wiki/J._Bruce_Ismay" title="J. Bruce Ismay">J. Bruce Ismay</a> of the <a href="/wiki/RMS_Titanic" title="RMS Titanic">Titanic</a>, was controversially disqualified, and the race was awarded to the 100/1 outsider Aboyeur. Suffragette <a href="/wiki/Emily_Davison" title="Emily Davison">Emily Davison</a> was struck by <a href="/wiki/George_V_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="George V of the United Kingdom">King George V</a>\'s horse, Anmer, she died four days later.</li>\n<li><b>1916</b>: <a href="/wiki/Fifinella_(horse)" title="Fifinella (horse)">Fifinella</a>, who also won <a href="/wiki/Epsom_Oaks" title="Epsom Oaks">The Oaks</a>, is the most recent (as of 2017) of six fillies to win the race. The previous five were Eleanor (1801), Blink Bonny (1857), Shotover (1882), Signorinetta (1908), Tagalie (1912).</li>\n<li><b>1921</b>: The winner Humorist died two weeks after the race.</li>\n<li><b>1927</b>: The first Derby to be broadcast by the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>.</li>\n<li><b>1932</b>: <a href="/wiki/April_the_Fifth" title="April the Fifth">April the Fifth</a> is the most recent winner trained at <a href="/wiki/Epsom" title="Epsom">Epsom</a>.</li>\n<li><b>1946</b>: Airborne is the most recent (as of 2017) of four grey horses to win the Derby.</li>\n<li><b>1953</b>: Pinza was the only winner in the race for the jockey <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Richards" title="Gordon Richards">Sir Gordon Richards</a>, after 27 unsuccessful attempts.</li>\n<li><b>1960</b>: Although there had been an experimental TV transmission of the race in the early 1930s, regular television coverage of the Derby began this year, initially on both <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> and <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a>.</li>\n<li><b>1967</b>: Starting stalls used for the first time.</li>\n<li><b>1989</b>: The runner-up <a href="/wiki/Terimon" title="Terimon">Terimon</a> is the longest-priced horse to finish placed in the Derby, at odds of 500/1.</li>\n<li><b>1996</b>: Alex Greaves became the first female jockey to ride in the race. She finished last of the 20 runners on the filly Portuguese Lil.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>1998</b>: The most recent (as of 2018) filly to take part, the <a href="/wiki/1,000_Guineas_Stakes" class="mw-redirect" title="1,000 Guineas Stakes">1,000 Guineas</a> winner Cape Verdi, started as 11/4 favourite but could only finish ninth.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>2006</b>: <a href="/wiki/Martin_Dwyer" title="Martin Dwyer">Martin Dwyer</a>\'s winning ride on <a href="/wiki/Sir_Percy" title="Sir Percy">Sir Percy</a> subsequently won the <a href="/wiki/Lester_Award" title="Lester Award">Lester Award</a> for "Flat Ride of the Year".<sup id="cite_ref-:2_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>2007</b>: <a href="/wiki/Authorized_(horse)" title="Authorized (horse)">Authorized</a> provided jockey <a href="/wiki/Frankie_Dettori" title="Frankie Dettori">Frankie Dettori</a> with his first winner in the Derby after 14 previous attempts.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>2008</b>: <a href="/wiki/Jim_Bolger_(racehorse_trainer)" title="Jim Bolger (racehorse trainer)">Jim Bolger</a>, the trainer of the winner <a href="/wiki/New_Approach" title="New Approach">New Approach</a>, had left the horse entered for the race "by mistake", having not initially intended to run.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>2010</b>: <a href="/wiki/Workforce_(horse)" title="Workforce (horse)">Workforce</a> broke the Epsom track record winning in the time 2m 31.33s previously held by <a href="/wiki/Lammtarra" title="Lammtarra">Lammtarra</a> who set it in 1995 at 2m 32.31s.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>2011</b>: <a href="/wiki/Pour_Moi" title="Pour Moi">Pour Moi</a> Jockey <a href="/wiki/Mickael_Barzalona" title="Mickael Barzalona">Mickael Barzalona</a> celebrated before the finishline winning by just a head.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>2012</b>: <a href="/wiki/Aidan_O%27Brien" title="Aidan O&#39;Brien">Aidan O\'Brien</a> and his 19-year-old son <a href="/wiki/Joseph_O%27Brien_(jockey)" title="Joseph O&#39;Brien (jockey)">Joseph</a> became the first father-son/trainer-jockey combination to win the race.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hayley_Turner" title="Hayley Turner">Hayley Turner</a> became the second female jockey to ride in the race, on Cavaleiro, finishing last of the nine horses which went to post, the lowest number since 1907.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>2014</b>: <a href="/wiki/Aidan_O%27Brien" title="Aidan O&#39;Brien">Aidan O\'Brien</a> became the first person to train three consecutive winners of the race.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>2017</b>: Ana O\'Brien, daughter of Aidan, was the third female jockey to ride in the race, on The Anvil. By finishing 17th of the 18 runners, she became the first woman to beat another runner to the line.<sup id="cite_ref-:9_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Epsom_Derby&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation"
